<!-- section 10 (id=5748, raw_sort=10): Ism -->
We're studing the Basmallah. and we've looked at the words Allah. AlRehman and AlRaheem in quite some detail over the last few sessions. What's left is the word Bism. So InshaAllah we'll study this word today and then wrap up our study of this ayah by bringing it all together.

Bism is actually two words. It is Ba combined with the word Ism. Ba is a preposition. One of its meanings is WITH. And then there is Ism. So the Basmallah is actually made up of 5 words. in which the first word "BISM" is a fusion of the Ba and the Ism. Now what does Ism mean?. In classical arabic Ism means noun. So there is ⟪ar:اسم⟫and ⟪ar:فعل⟫. noun and verb. The second meaning of Ism is. name. So one meaning is noun. and the other meaning is name. And the reason for that.  is because every noun . has a name. right?. Anything and everything that is a noun. always has a name. There is an animal. which is a noun. and then it has a name. lion, tiger, dog, cat. An object is a noun. and so it has a name. table, chair, fan, computer. These are all names. So noun. and name. they both go hand in hand. That's why Ism . in classical Arabic. means both things.

Now what's SO interesting about this statement. Bismillah. With the name of Allah.  is that we can aruge that the word Ism is completely unnecessary. It's redundant. Because we talked about this in detail. that Allah itself is a name. It is the name of the divine essence. So I could say instead. باللہ الرحمن الرحیم. and I would not be missing anything in meaning. After all we say. اعوذ باللہ . I seek refuge of Allah all the time. We don't say. اعوذ بسم اللہ . I seek refuge with the name of Allah. Because I need refuge of Allah. not his name. So then why do I have to say بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم. when I could easily say. باللہ الرحمن الرحیم. and it would mean the same thing? . If I'm working on a project with Nadia. when it's done. I'm not going to say. I completed this project with the name of Nadia. right?. I completed this project with Nadia. You get the point. I don't have to say with the NAME of Nadia. right? .

Similarly the word Allah can be used with the Ba. without the Ism. In fact. it is used all over the place in the Quran . all the time.

وَمِنَ ٱلنَّاسِ مَن يَقُولُ آمَنَّا بِٱللَّهِ

not آمنا بسم اللہ .

يَحْلِفُونَ بِٱللَّهِ

They swear by Allah. not ⟪ar:يَحْلِفُونَ بِسم للَّهِ⟫. They swear by the name of Allah. you understand?

So then why is the word Ism being used here?. The ONLY conclusion we can draw. by the usage of the word Ism here. is that it is not actually referring to the Allah itself. It must be referring to something else.  Because if it was talking about the name Allah. then it would be completely redundant. which would create a linguistic imperfection . and this Quran would no longer be the linguistic miracle that it claims to be. which is impossible. So we need to understand why Allah has used that word ISM in this ayah. And this is a topic of taveel. but I've especially asked Javeed bhai for permission to share this with you.

---

ISM - NAMES

Now since the beginning of time. since the creation of the first man. the concept of name has been extremely important. In fact the Quran highlights the importance of names. in the story of the creation of Adam AS. Because name. was the ONE thing that elevated Adam AS in rank. and it gave him preference OVER the angels. If you remember the story. When Allah decides to create Adam AS. all the angels have a problem with that. right off the bat. They argue with Allah. they challenge his decision.
⟪ar-quote:وَإِذْ قَالَ رَبُّكَ لِلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ إِنِّى جَاعِلٌۭ فِى ٱلْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةًۭ ۖ⟫

When your master told the angles that I'm going to create my representative on earth.
⟪ar-quote:قَالُوٓا۟ أَتَجْعَلُ فِيهَا مَن يُفْسِدُ فِيهَا وَيَسْفِكُ ٱلدِّمَآءَ⟫

They said. Do you really want to create someone who will do mischief in the earth and spill blood?
⟪ar-quote:وَنَحْنُ نُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِكَ وَنُقَدِّسُ لَكَ⟫

If praise and gratitude and glory is all that you want. we are all enough for that.  And then Allah says to them.
⟪ar-quote:قَالَ إِنِّىٓ أَعْلَمُ مَا لَا تَعْلَمُونَ⟫

I know that which you do not know. And then in response to that challenge. what is the VERY next thing that Allah does?.

⟪ar-quote:وَعَلَّمَ آدَمَ ٱلْأَسْمَآءَ كُلَّهَا⟫

So Allah taught Adam AS. Names. His 99 divine names. You see!.
⟪ar-quote:ثُمَّ عَرَضَهُمْ عَلَى ٱلْمَلَٓئِكَةِ  ⟪ar-quote:فَقَالَ⟫⟫

And so then Allah presented Adam AS to all the angels. and said.
⟪ar-quote:أَنۢبِـُٔونِى بِأَسْمَآءِ هَٓؤُلَآءِ إِن كُنتُمْ صَدِقِينَ⟫

Now you guys tell me these NAMES. if you are truthful.

And they couldn't answer. The angels couldn't answer.  because they did not know the NAMES. because THEY. were NOT the ones who were taught the names. Only Adam. was taugh the names. And so what made him worthy of prostration. was exactly that. NAMES. So NAME.  is an EXTREMELY important concept that was given ONLY to Adam AS. and which elevated his rank over the rank of angels. And after Adam AS. this is something that was given to us. Because we are Banee Adam. We are the children of Adam.

Now what is name?. Name is the ability of symbolic thought.  That is the essence of naming.  Naming something. is taking a symbol.  which is linguistic in nature.  and then applying it to something which is either material or empirical that we can feel. Or a name is something that we can use as an abstraction. to create separation in things.  See Animals cannot do that.  Animals cannot use symbolic language. 

It has been agreed by the Arab scholars. that human beings have basically three dominant modes of symbolic language.  we have linguistics which is the highest.  and then we have mathematics which actually comes under linguistics. As I said the last time. the 20th century.  or really the Western civilization. has elevated mathematics OVER language. Language has taken a secondary place. because they don't understand the power of Arabic. And even the muslims today. they too try to place mathematics OVER the Quran. when it comes to proving the Quran as a miracle. And no doubt Quran is mathematically perfect.  and I've shown you quite a few examples of that by now.  but it is still primarily a linguistic miracle and not a mathematical one.  This need to prove the Quran mathematically is based on this feeling of inferiority before the God of modern science.  which is mathematics.  And this comes from Newton and Einstein and all these other people who elevated mathematics. and said that it is the only real way of understanding reality.  Because mathematics is precise and exact.  But then these people did not study classical Arabic. Because Arabic is precise and exact . And it is precise and exact in a way. that mathematics cannot come close to.  and this is why the miracle of Quran. the Ejaz. the mojiza of Quran. is not in its mathematics. It is in its linguistics. Quran is a linguistic miracle. And the recognition of this linguistic miracle comes from our ablitity to recognize things through names.

Language unifies

This is the secret of the human beings. that we have the ability to abstract, differentiate. identify.  through names. We as human beings. we have the ability to see the *ONE* in the many. That's the ONLY way we can communicate. Think about it. The only way we can communicate is by seeing the one in the many. When we talk about a lecture. for example when I tell you.  that there is going to be a session next Sunday at 9:30 am. How do you know what a session means in this context?. Because the word SESSION has many meanings in different contexts. For example I could say…. this is a religious session. school is in session. the courtroom is in session. Yasmeen had a great tennis coaching session. the Federal Act was passed in the session of 1908. So the word session has so many different meanings in various different context. So when I say there's going to be a session on Sunday.  How do you know. what meaning of the word session I'm talking about. that this is going to be a religious sesson?. And how do you know exactly which Sunday I'm talking about.  because a month has 4 weeks. and each week has a Sunday. Every Sunday has a 9:30 am. So out of all these multiple meanings for these words….  Sunday and sessions.  you are able to extract ONE particular meaning. understand it…. and then show up on the correct day at the correct time for the correct reasons.  This is the ability we human beings have .  This is because we have the capablity to abstract the one …. out of the many. And when we are not able to do this. when we are not able to zero-in on THE one particular meaning. we are forced to say. Wait a minute. Just want to make sure. Did you mean this coming Sunday. or the one after that. or the one after that?. Because every sentence needs to boil down to one particular thought from a sea of possibilities.

And so what this enables us to do. is speak intelligently about the oneness. and the unified nature of words. Because that's who we are. We are all unifiers by nature. This is what we do as human beings. We are ⟪ar:موحدون⟫.  we are constantly making one out of the many.  And how do we do that?. How do we make one?. We do that through language. We can only communicate because of the oneness of language. And so through names. we were given this gift of unification. so that we could perform the ultimate unification. Tawheed. That's what the word Tawheed means. Unification. Tawheed comes from the root word "Hadd". which means boundary. or a confine. And hadd is the root word for "Wahid". which means ONE. and also Ahad. which means unique. So Tawheed. Ahad. and Wahid. they all come from Hadd. which means a boundary. And what does a boundary give you?. It gives you one distinct entity. It separates the one from the many.

So this ability to unify things through language. is a sign. that we have been created to perform the ultimate abstraction. and the ultimate unification. It is to recognize.  that this diverse creation also has to have a single and unique source.  Just as we can abstract the essence of the word session.  out of all these diverse meanings for the word. we can also abstract the essence of existence.  out of all this diversity around us.  and the essence of existence is Allah (Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala).  He is our master of all creation. because he is the CREATOR of all creation. and it is only THROUGH his creation. that we can identify him. This identification. This unification is the purpose of creation.
⟪ar-quote:وما خلقت الجن و الانس الا لیعبدون⟫

And we did not create jinn and man except for Ibadah. And Ibadaha or worship. necessititates the extraction of the one ILAH. from multiple Ilah. That's what truly lies at the heart of Ibadah. The unification of the Ilah. Choosing the ONE from the many. And this is how you reach Allah. La Ilaha Illa . Allah. That's the ultimate abstraction. that's the ultimate unification. From multiple ilah. you get THE ONE ILAH. and that is Allah. That is tawheed. and this tawheed. this unification. is the heart and soul of Ibadah. the worship we were created for.

So the Basmallah begins . بسم اللہ. with the name of Allah. because we know Allah through the power of symbolic understanding.  We cannot know Allah as we know things.  we cannot know Allah the way we know a tape recorder. or a laptop or a computer. Because essences are hard to understand.  even with things.  but when it comes to Allah. it becomes absolutely impossible. The only way we can know Allah is through symbolic language. which is his 99 divine names. or divine attributes. Because Allah HAS NO likeness. He has no misaal.

### Purpose of example

See. masal. is an analogical symbol for something that we already know. to let us know something that we do not know. If you understand something that you already know. a person can explain to you.  using that example.  something that you do not know. And you say. Aaaah I got it!. it's LIKE this. . But when it comes to Allah. ⟪ar:لیس کمثلہ شئی⟫.  right? . Allah has no equivalent likeness.

And so we have these 99 divine names. as linguistic symbols. so we can have some concept of who he is. So for example. Allah is called . ⟪ar:مالک یوم الدین⟫. Owner or King of the day of judgement. Now because we understand Malik. because we understand the concept of a king. we can now relate to the position that Allah will take on the day of judgement.  the position of a king. the position of the ultimate owner. We can understand that through that symbolic reference. But we know now that Allah is not limited to our concept of what a king means. He is way more exalted than that. But whatever concept we have is enough to get the point across.

So there is this distinction between Allah. and the names of Allah. There is a distinction between Ism and Allah. The names of Allah. because of our ability to use names as symbolic thoughts. they allow us to understand and identify Allah. Because that is the ONLY purpose of a name. to identify the noun. My name is Asif. When you kids hear my name. you are able to uniquely identify my essence. And you go.  Ahhh. Its that guy who tortures me for an hour every Sunday.

---

So name is a symbol for abstraction. Name is a symbol for identification. Names help identify nouns. That's why the the word Ism means both things. name and noun. because names help identify nouns. So if you keep this concept in mind. and NOW if you read the Basmallah. And again. we're venturing into Taveel at this point. So this is not common knowledge. this is something that is specific to the knowledge that we Sulemani's possess. OK?

So . بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم. With the name of Allah. who is AlRehman and AlRaheem. That's the common translation. But in the language of taveel. we can now translate this as.

With the nouns who can identify Allah for us. Listen carefully. With the nouns who can help identify Allah for us. what about Allah? His Rehmaniyat and His Raheemiyat for us. So BARR. With the nouns. These nouns are certain VERY specific . chosen people. who can identify. clarify. explain. Allah's Rehmaniyat and Raheemiyat FOR us. That's why the word Ism is specifically used in this verse. To highlight these people. who can explain to us . transmit to us the knowledge. of how Allah is AlRehman and AlRaheem.

Now who are these people?. and how many are they?. Well how many words are there in the Basmallah?. There are 5 words in the Basmallah. Ba + Ism + Allah + AlRehman + AlRaheem. These represent the 5 people. that Allah has chosen. to explain the Rehmaniyat and Raheemiyat of Allah. to clarify his intense mercy and his permanent mercy to us. These are who we know as the Panjatan-e-Paak. Muhammad + Ali + Fatima + Hassan and Hussain. These are the Ahlul Bait. the members of the house of Rasul Allah. who have been chosen to show us Allah's Rehmaniyat AND his Raheemiyat. both conceptually as well as practically.

If you're not convinced. Count the letters in the names of the panjatan. Muhammad (4) + Ali (3) + Fatima (5) + Hassan (3) + Hussain (4). That's 19. Count the letters of the Basmallah. They're 19 as well.

If you're still not convinced. Look at the letters of the Basmallah. They fall into 2 categories. There are the repeating letters . and the non-repeating letters. And they too are 5 in number. There are 5 repeating letters. and 5 non-repeating letters. I'm not going to go into the taveel of who the non-repeating ones are. But for now understand. that the repeating 5 are the Panjatan Paak.

Just like in the kalima. la ilaha illa Allah. you have to categories. which also contain 5 repetiions. You have the Alif which is repeated 5 times. and you have the Laam which is repeated 5 times. And this because there is a direct relationship between the Basmallah and the Kalima Ikhlaas.

So Ism in the Basmallah. represent the 5 nouns. or the 5 people. the panjatan. who are the true names of Allah. because they are the ONLY ones who can identify Allah's attributes for us. especially the attributes of AlRehman and AlRaheem. So the presence of the word Ism there. is to indicate that if you try to approach Allah. without the guidance of these 5 chosen people. you will not be able to understand the love. the care. the concern. and the mercy of Allah. Not in this life. Not in the after life.

---

Now that we've coverd the individual words. let's understand the entire ayah. We are told to recite this ayah BEFORE every single act that we do. Even the act of revelation. When the first ayah was revealed on Rasul Allah (SAS) . what phrase did it contain?.
⟪ar-quote:اقرأ باسم ربک الذی خلق⟫

Read. with the name of your master who created you.

it really is the essence of the phrase. now in this case the verb comes first. why? Because it is the beginning of the Quranic revelation. and notice that the name Allah is missing from this ayah. It says اقرأ باسم ربک: it does not say اقرأ باسم اللہ: That's why the verb came first in this ayah. but whenever the most glorious name "Allah" is mentioned, the verb always comes after the name Allah. it is always a subsequent verb.

For example when Allah commanded Nooh to board the ship what did he say?

وَقَالَ ٱرْكَبُوا۟ فِيهَا بِسْمِ ٱللَّهِ مَجْر۪ىٰهَا وَمُرْسَىٰهَآ

Allah said to Nooh (AS). go and ride on the ship . and when you get on it. say bismillah. before you actually begin riding it. so the verb or riding the ship comes after bismillah because the name Allah is mentioned in this ayah

and when prophet Sulaiman wrote to the queen of sheebah. and when that letter is read out to her. what did the letter say?

إِنَّهُۥ مِن سُلَيْمَنَ وَإِنَّهُۥ بِسْمِ ٱللَّهِ ٱلرَّحْمَنِ ٱلرَّحِيمِ

This letter is from Sulaiman. and before it is read out. it begins with BARR. then the letter is read out to her. the verb again comes after the bismillah. because they ayah contains the name Allah.

And we know that whenever Rasul Allah (Salawaat) would begin a task. he would begin by reciting Bismillah AlRehman AlRaheem. He would begin his lectures. his khutbas. his salaah. Anything he did. he would begin with BARR . and in one hadees he says
⟪ar-quote:کلُّ أمرٍ ذِی بَال لَم یُبدَأ بِسم اللہِ تَعالیٰ . فَھُوَ أَقْطَعْ فَھُوَ أَجْزَمْ⟫

That every single deed of importance that does not begin by saying bismillah. it is as if the deed has been amputated. it is not whole . it is ugly.  or it is mutliated.

Every single deed of importance that does not begin with bismillah. then it is ⟪ar:اقطع⟫it is cutoff. it is ⟪ar:اجزم⟫it is mutilated.

Thats why we say bismillah before eveyrthing of importance that we do.

Even when rasul Allah (Salawaat) would write letters to the non-muslim kings. For example when Heracleus.  the emperor of Rome. received a letter from Rasul Allah (SAS). and when the translator opened up the letter and read it. the first thing it had was.
⟪ar-quote:بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم۔ من محمدٍ رسول اللہ الی حِرَقَل العظیم الرُّوم⟫

BARR. this is a letter from Muhammad the messenger of Allah to Hiraqal the emperor of Rome. So you see even when he begin a written document. he began it with BARR!

---

Why recite BARR before every action?

Now let's see what that is. Why do we say the Basmallah BEFORE beginning any action.

If we think about this translation of the Basmallah. With the NAME of Allah. who is AlReheman  and AlRehman. If you just look at this sentence. even without knowing any arabic grammar. you can immediately tell that this is an incomplete sentence. With the name of Allah. With the name of Allah WHAT?  . What with the name of Allah? And even from a grammatical standpoint the BA is a preposition. therefore by rule. it has to be associated with something. it has to be associated with either a noun or a verb. Because a preposition cannot just exist by itself. So WITH the name of Allah WHAT? . What am I doing with the name of Allah? . So its obvious that something is missing here.

And if you look at each of these words grammatically. Bism is a preposition combined with a noun. Allah is a proper noun.  AlRehman and AlRaheem are adjectives. So you have a prepo. you have a noun. and you have adjectives. So then grammatically what is missing here?. What's missing here. is a verb. It is missing what they call a PERTINENT and SUBSEQUENT verb. the scary lingo for that is. ⟪ar:جار والمجرور متعلق بہ و متأخر بہ⟫. So I'm sure that makes sense to everyone. Moving on . I'm kidding. I'll explain.

OK. so what's missing from the Basmallah. is a verb that is pertinent. ⟪ar:متعلق بہ⟫ and that is subsequent. ⟪ar:و متأخر بہ⟫

Let's lets look at the pertinent verb first. ⟪ar:متعلق بہ⟫ . You kids know what pertinent means right?. Something related to the matter at hand. something relevant.

First of all. why is it missing a verb in the first place?. 

Because verbs are actions. Actions are not normally nouns.  Actions are verbs.  So my action. the action that I am about to perform . after reciting this ayah. it provides the missing verb and the context of my action. THUS completing the sentence. You understand?. The reason the Basmallah is missing the VERB. is because I have to provide the verb by my action. 

So when I say.⟪ar:بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم⟫. and then I start reading a book.  the action of reading.  provides the missing verb.  the missing context. and that then completes the sentence of  BARR. And so what the ayah transforms into is. With the name of Allah who is Rehman AlRaheem.  I am reading this book. With the name of Allah who is Rehman AlRaheem.  I am entering my house. With the name of Allah who is Rehman AlRaheem. I am drinking this glass of water. With the name of Allah who is Rehman AlRaheem.  I am beginning this exam.  So my action provides the pertinent verb.  the context.  that was grammatically missing from the original sentence of BARR. And so my action then completes the sentence grammatically.

This is the reason why the verb is missing from the original sentence. So that WE put in the verb through our action.  If Allah had added the verb Himself.  If Allah had made the verb a part of the ayah.  then we could not use this ayah for anything . OTHER than what Allah used it for. If allah had said: ⟪ar:بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم أتلوٰ ھذا القرآن⟫. With the name of Allah I recite this Quran. then the verb.  would have been TIED to the sentence itself.  and we could not be able to use this ayah for any other action. EXCEPT for reciting the quran. So Allah (Subhanhu Wa Ta'ala)  eliminated the verb from this ayah.  so that we could use this sentence before every action we perform in our daily lives. So that's the meaning of the pertinent verb.  ⟪ar:متعلق بہ⟫

Now what was the other thing I said? A pertinent verb and what?.  A subsequent verb.  Now what does subsequent mean?. Something that comes later.  ⟪ar:متأخر بہ⟫.   So for example if I want to recite the Basmallah. before reciting the Quran.  I can say it in 2 ways.  I can say.  I recite in the name of Allah.  or I can say.  in the name of Allah I recite. I can put the verb recite. before the name of Allah by saying.  I RECITE with the name of allah. ⟪ar:أقرأُ بسم اللہ⟫.  In this case I put the verb recite first. OR I can put the verb. AFER the name of Allah by saying . With the name of Allah I RECITE . ⟪ar:بسم اللہ أقرأ⟫. Now whats the difference? who cares if it is before or after?. Who cares if it is I recite with the name of Allah.  or With the name of Allah i recite. Tomatoes. Tamotoes. right?  Who cares? . Well actually we do care . and we care for 2 reasons.

1. We always want to mention the name of Allah first. Because as I explained. the 99 names.  are symbolic representations of Allah's divine essence. So we call upon the name of Allah first. to bind our action. which is yet to come. within the confines of his attributes. It is a call for Allah's help. It is a dua. asking Allah. that the action that I am about to perform. make it a manifestation of your divine attributes. And include your Rehma. your love. your care. your genuine concern. and your infinite mercy . with my action. So by making my action subsequent. by delaying my action. AFTER calling upon the names of Allah. I am doing two things.

First . I am calling upon Allah's help in making my action a divine manifestation of one of his divine attributes. by including his Rehma within my action. and

Second. I am glorifying and honoring Allah. by calling upon him.  BEFORE my action. in order to remind myself. that He is my master. and I am his slave. So I remind myself that Allah is my true north. Therefore this action that I am about to perform. it MUST be in accordance to HIS will and HIS command. That's the first reason why we care to make the action subsequent.

The second reason. and this we cannot do in English. so we need to understand this one in Arabic itself.  In arabic. the reason we delay the verb. is to imply exclusivity.  Its called ⟪ar:الحصر . In⟫Arabic when I place the verb first. If I say. I recite this Quran with the name of Allah.  then this does not eliminate the fact that I could be reciting for other reasons as well. Its possible I could be reciting to show off.  I could be reciting to make sure my neighbours don't sleep. I could be reciting because I want to get paid for my recitiation.  I could be reciting because of this.  because of that. .  But in Arabic. when you place the verb. AFTER the noun. When I say. ⟪ar:بسم اللہ أقرأ⟫.  then what that means is. I am reciting.  ONLY for the sake of Allah. There is no other reason that I am reciting. You understand?

When we push the verb to the end. we add a clause of exclusivity with the action.  The ONLY reason I am reciting.  The ONLY reason I am entering the house.  The only reason I am drinking this glass of water. the only reason I am giving this exam. is EXCLUSIVELY FOR Allah. who is AlRehman and AlRaheem.  I have not other diety. no other god in mind. So this is why the verb must be subsequent.

So that's the reason the Basmallah is recited before every action. because it is missing the contextual VERB. which I provide by my action. And the verb must also be subsequent to call upon Allah's help. asking him to include his Rehma with the task I am about to perform. to glorify him. and then also to remind myself that I am do this task EXCLUSIVELY for Allah. And this produces sincerity. IKHLAAS.  in the action that I am about to perform. I am not doing this to show off. I am not doing this for praise. I am not doing this for any reason . OTHER than to please my master. and that I am in complete need of his love. his care. his concern and his mercy in order to complete this task to the standard that HE would be pleased with me.

---

BA of BISMILLAH

Now what does the preposition "BA" mean?. The BA has several gramatical implications. The first is intention. I am putting the intention of pleasing Allah before I even begin the task. I am setting the pleasure of Allah as my goal.  And when the goal is clear.  when the priorities are clear. the proper subsequent actions automatically and naturally fall into place. And this is why the messenger said.

⟪ar-quote:انما الاعمال بالنیات⟫

No doubt. the actions will ONLY be judged on the basis of intention. So when I open up the book of Allah. and I say BARR.  I am saying. Oh Allah. I am begining with your name. I am beginning with you in mind. Seeking YOUR pleasure is the end goal of my recitation. With this I wish to come closer to you. And so the intention here. is being placed before the action as proof of sincerity.

The second reason is that the Baa indicates the desire for companionship. When I say BARR. BEFORE begining my task.  I am saying.  Oh Allah. I need you on my side for this task. I need you to be with me. This is called ⟪ar:الباء لی المصاحبۃ⟫.  I want Allah (Azza Wa Jal) to be with me.  I want his Rehmaniyat.  his Raheemiyat to be with me.  It is the admission of a weak and humble slave. towards his ALL powerful master. That I cannot do this task without you Oh Allah!.  If you do not help me in this task that I am about to do. I will not be able to do it. I will not succeed in it. If you do not help me get to work in the morning. I cannot get to work in the morning.  If you do not help me pass this exam. I cannot pass this exam. So Bismillah. Oh Allah with your help. I wish to begin.  what I am about to begin. so that I can accomplish the final goal. which is to meet with your approval. So this is the ba of Musahiba. or companionship.

Now generally in life we don't see that. I mean I see that I don't say BARR.  and yet my tasks complete without any problems. You must have succeeded numerous times without saying BARR. So then what's up?.

Well this again goes back to the difference between ALRehman and ALRaheem. Like I said in the earlier sessions. Rehman is general love and mercy. The Rehman gives to all. whether they call upon Allah or not. believers or disbelievers. doesn't matter. But Raheem is a very special kind of mercy that is ONLY for the believers.

Then the love and mercy of Rehman is ONLY for THIS life. but the love and mercy of the Raheem is for the after life. So if I succeed in my task without saying BARR. it is because of the Rehman. But I will have not reward for that worldly task in the after life.  So for example if I am beginning a task at work or school. and this is not a religious task. it is a worldly task. but because I called upon Allah for it. a reward from the Raheem has now been made obligatory for me. The REHMAN may help me succeed in the task regardless. and I'll get praise and reward for that task by my teacher or my boss in THIS world. but this task will not give me any benefit in the after life. But if I called upon Allah. with both his names of love. AlReham and AlRheem. then the Rehman may or may not let me succeed in the task of this world. but the Raheem will DEFINITELY reward me for it in the afterlife. This is a VERY VERY important thing to remember. Just imagine how many actions. worldly actions we do in a day. Just by remembering Allah. by saying BARR. that same action can turn into worship. So this is something we all must try very hard to discipline ourselves into. And another reason how remembering Allah before an action helps.  is that we would never commit a sin after reciting BARR. Just Fitratan. naturally we would not be able to do that. And if we did actually that. Even after reciting BARR. we would still commit a sin. then that completely change our stance. We would not stand in opposition to Allah. Because we are now saying.  Oh Allah. even though I am aware of your glory. Even though I am aware of your strength.  I am still committing this sin. Do what you can! نعوذ باللہ من ذالک . But as a believer. Even just as a decent human being. this ayah cannot even reach our lips if we are about to commit a sin. So if we are in the habit of reciting BARR before everything we do. it will serve as a strong reminder.  and a powerful guardian.  that will portect us from committing sins.

And the final reason for reciting BARR. And this is exclusively for our religious deeds. is ⟪ar:البائُنَا القبول⟫ . The BA of Allah's acceptance. Even though we do want Allah to be pleased with our worldly deeds. We ESPECIALLY want him to accept our religious deeds. Because they both do not weigh the same on the scales on the day of judgment. So reciting the Basmallah. is not just calling upon Allah with sincerity. with true intention. asking for his help and companionship. it is also for his final acceptance. Because if Allah does not accept my act. then it's like I never did the act. Imagine you work extremely hard on a project for months. You work night and day on it. And the purpose was that it would go towards your final grades. But on the final day you find out that your project is not being graded. How disappointed would you be?. It's the same thing here. All the religious actions of worship that we are doing. we pray . we fast. we give zakaat. we do all of this stuff and then on the day of judgment if these acts are not accepted. what would be the level of our disappointment and grief?. And that's what the Ba of the Basmallah does for us. It is saying.  Oh Allah.  I want your acceptance for my deed.  I want you to accept my effort of this worship. becauuse I am doing it with sincerity. and with the intention to please you. seeking your companionship and help. I want my action to elevate and rise up to you.

---

Purpose of BASMALLAH is BARAKAH

And now finally. what is the effect of the Basmallah?. We saw the reasons. we saw the purpose. Now the final question. How does the Basmallah help the task at hand?. What benefit does BARR provide to me in the action that I am about to perform. That benefit is Barakah. which is commonly translated as abundance. There is a hadees that the prophet narrates. in which Allah says.

⟪ar-quote:أنی اذا اُطِعتُ رَضِیتُ. وأذا رَضِیتُ بَارَکتُ. وَ لَیسَ لِبَرَکَتِی نِھَایَۃ⟫

When you obey me it pleases me. when I am pleased. I give you barakh. and there is no limit to my barkah.  Also in the Quran . In Surah AlRehman. Allah says.

⟪ar-quote:تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ ذِى ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ⟫

The name of your glorious and benevolent master. . is full of barakah.  The name of Allah. is full of barakah.⟪ar:تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ⟫.  So all the divine names of Allah are full of Barakah. And then in another verse he says.

But Allah does not mention in this ayah. which name is full of barakah. right? It just said the name of your maser is full of Barakah. But what did this surah begin with? AlRehman! And what is the first attribute of Allah mentioned in the Basmallah? Bismillahi. AL-REHMAN.  AlRaheem. So Allah is telling us something about the word AlRehman. In Surah Rehaman. allah is saying that this name of Allah that I began with. meaning AlRehman. is full of barakah.

But we also know that Allah himself is full of barakah. Because he says it in the Quran.

⟪ar-quote:تبرک اللہ احسن الخالقین⟫

Your Allah is full of barakh who is the best of creators!

In this ayah. he associates barakh with himself. not with his name. So we find both flavors in the Quran. the name of the essence. Allah. is full of barakh. and then all of his divine names are also full of barakah.

but in this last ayah of Surah AlRehman . he's not saying تبرک اللہ . he's not talking about himself. He is talking about his name. He says. تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ  . The name . AlRehman. of your master is full of Barakah. So Allah is full of Barakah. and His name AlRehman is full of barakah. you understand? Now when we recite the Basmallah. do we have these two names in that ayah? Bismi ALLAHI ALREHMAN AlRaheem. Both Allah and AlRehman. both names of Barakah . is used in the Basmallah.

So the reason we recite the Basmallah. The reason we mention Allah's name before beginnig a task.  is for Barakah.Why?. Because the Basmallah is OVER-FLOWING with Allah's names. We have the bism. And we just saw that the ism has barakah. .تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ. The name of your master is full of barakah.  The second word is Allah. and we saw. تبرک اللہ. the name of the essence. Allah. is also full of barakah. And then we have two explicit names. AlRheman and Raheem. which are also of barakah because they both are from the divine names. So you can see that this ayah. comprises of words that are over flowing with barakah. and so when we recite this ayah before any task that we do. it spills out that barakah into the task that we are about to perform. And so by reciting the Basmallah before every task. we are intentionally asking Allah to bless the task with the barakah of his names in the Basmallah.

Now there is no word in the English language that can fully encmpass the meaning of the word Barakah.  So we need to understand this word barakah. through certain concepts. In Arabaic. Barakah is defined as.

⟪ar-quote:البرکۃُ النَّماَءُ وَ الزِّیَادَۃ⟫

The first meaning of barakh is growth. Something that rises. something that increases. makes progress. something that goes further and further and increases ⟪ar:فوق التوقع⟫. beyond expectations.  If you plant a seed in the ground.  how many trees do you expect? Just one! But if you put one seed in the ground. and you get 10 trees. with fruits producing hundreds of thousands of seeds. THAT is barakah. You planted one seed and eventually got thousands of seeds. that's a growth beyond expectations. That is what you call barakah.  Barakah means. logic says I should get one tree but I got a whole forest. how did that happen? That's barakah. Also . what is the comparison of a tree with a seed?.  There is no comparison. It is beyond comparison. Because a seed is tiny. a tree is huge. a seed is delicate. a tree is strong. a seed has no value. a tree bears hundreds upon hundreds of fruits.  season after season after season. for years and years . If you really think about it. what we get from a tree. compared to a seed. there is no comparison. Yet that entire tree came from that one seed. SubhanAllah! That is barakah. unprecedented growth. unlimited increase.

The Arabs say. ⟪ar:أبتَرَکَتِ السَّمَآء⟫ means when rain keeps on coming and keeps on coming.  so CONTINUITY is another characteristic of the word barakah. Something that stays continuous.

You cook food for 2 people. suddenly 10 guests show up at your door. You all sit down to eat. and from that same food for 2 people. 12 people eat and they leave completely satisified. That is barakah. That's not logical. you only cooked for 2 people. it should not have been enough to satisfy 12 people. but it completely satisfied them. how did that happen? That's barakah. This acutally happened during the time of Ali bin Sydena Suleman QR. There was a wedding in the house of this man who wasn't very well off. He invited a few people from his village to attend the wedding. but word spread and two villages gathered for the wedding. This man got really worried . so he came to Syedna Ali bin Syedna Suleman and explained what happened. He said I don't have enough food to feed them all. Syedna Ali said. go back and recite the name of Syenda Suleman 3 times in each cauldron. A few hours later that man returns to Syedna Ali with a big tray of food in his hand. Syedna Ali asks him. what happened?. He said. Syedee. I did what you told me to do. and everyone ate from the food and left completely satisified and still there is food left over for my family. so I brought some of it for you. This is barakah. This is one of 1000 documented miracles of Syedna Suleman QR. Because the name Suleman has barakah. why? because as the Quran says.

⟪ar-quote:إِنَّهُۥ مِن سُلَيْمَنَ وَإِنَّهُۥ بِسْمِ ٱللَّهِ ٱلرَّحْمَنِ ٱلرَّحِيمِ⟫

I started this session with 5 people. and I did 12 sessions. Now MashaAllah I have more poeple in the group than skype allows. and we're on our 45th session. How did that happen? I did not do anything.  I did not go out inviting people. Yet I ended up with so many more poeople in the group. This is barakah. why? Because what are we doing in these session?. We are mentioning Allah's name. because we are talking about Allah and AlRehman and AlRaheem.

So the meaning of barakah is growth.  or increase beyond expectations. Barakah is also used in the Arabic language. for example the Arab would say. ⟪ar:أِذا أَناَخَ الْجَمَل⟫ . When the camel settles on the ground. and it doesn't move or budge. That is also barakah. And this is really beautifull.  Because when you grow something.  and you grow it too much.  I'll give an example so you can understand. when kids play with legos. they build up this huge tower. which is just block upon block upon block right?.  Now as the tower is getting tall. does it become more stable? or does it become less stable?.  It becomes less stable. The taller the tower. the less stable it becomes. It will eventually fall and break. and there will be no tower anymore. isn't that true?

So when something increases rapidly.  and increase too much. it becomes less stable. But when something has barakah. it means. that something will increases. and keep increasing beyond expectations. yet remains as stable as a camel sunk in the sand. SubhanAllah!  In other words don't think this increase will go away. its not an unstable increase.

We know about unstable increase when we look all around us. our economy goes up really fast. and then what happens? It comes down really fast. there are governments that take over really fast. and then disappear really fast as well. Look at the fashion industry.  there are trends that pickup really fast. and then disappear just as fast. something else takes its place. But Allah says barakah is when something increases.  but it remains stable. it stays constant. it doesnt go away.

And when Allah says his name is full of barakh. what does that mean? . It means Allah's names. and AlRehman's name is being mentioned. since the day creation came into existence. and it only increases and grows with every single passing moment. and it will continue to grow till the very end of creation. Allah and his name.  will remain forever. because they are full of barakah. Worshipers come and go. but the one that is worshipped remains. People who glorify the names of Allah come and go. many came before us. many will come after us. we will all go away. but the glory of Allah will ALWAYS remain.  This is the barakh of Allah's name.

And what does this mean to us? How do we take advanatage of this in our daily lives? It means that when we mention Allah's name. when we recite the basmallah. that contains names that are full of barakah. when we call upon the barakah of these names. then whatever we do.  it will produce good. and it will produce good that will be more than expected.  its growth will continue. and it will not disappear. Not only that. it will also be stable. It will keep going and going and going.

Because of this Basmallah. scholars say. that everyone single muslim is supposed to be an optimist. EVEN if the task at hand apparently fails. from that failure there will be growth. the temporary failure will produce spiritual growth and lead to bigger and better tasks.

And because the name of Allah was mentioned before we started the task.  with the intention of calling upon his barakah. that task will be recorded in our book of deeds. and its reward will keep accumulating for the after life. And this is because the very mention of the name of Allah has now made it an act of worship. so now if it takes me 10 hours to complete that task. I just did 10 hours of worship. Just by reciting the Basmallah at the beginning of the task. the time it takes me to complete it . is earning me rewards. And after I have completed the task. the effect of what I've produced is going to keep earning rewards for me as long as it is fulfilling its purpose. Just think about that. Reciting one basmallah. with the right intention. and look at the amount of reward it accumulates. So Basmallah before a task. is the seed of barakah that we plant. which then blossoms into thousands upon thousands of trees bearing uncountable fruits of rewards for us. SubhanAllah!

Every single good deed is an act of barakah. You may help one single person. You may teach one single person. and you don't know. what if that person ends up becoming a great scholar?. He ends up teaching thousands of students. and you keep getting a share of his reward in all his accomplishments. As long as he is teaching and students are benefitting from him. you keep accumulating reward. And then some of those students beome teachers and they spread that knowledge. and the reward for ALL of this is accumulating in your book of deeds. because all of this started with the seed you planted. because you started that person on his journey. This is barakah!

And so we cannot calculate the results that stem from the Basmallah. Because they are from Allah. and they will grow and grow beyond human expectation. beyond common sense. beyond logic. Mathematics cannot capture that number. it cannot encompass it.

SABAHA and TABARAKA used with Allah

If we study the Quran. what we find is that it tells us to make tasbeeh to Allah . and to the name of allah.

⟪ar-quote:سَبَّحَ لِلَّهِ مَا فِى ٱلسَّمَوَتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ⟫

Everything in the heavens and the earth glorifies Allah. and we also find.

⟪ar-quote:سَبِّحِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ ٱلْأَعْلَى⟫

We glorify the NAME of Allah

Then we find the same patter with ⟪ar:تبارک⟫. which means "blessed". This word is also used directly with Allah. and it is also used with the name of Allah

⟪ar-quote:فَتَبَارَكَ ٱللَّهُ أَحْسَنُ ٱلْخَلِقِينَ⟫

and

⟪ar-quote:تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ ذِى ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ⟫

So the word tabarak is used directly with Allah and also with the name of Allah

Also. the Quran tells us to remember Allah.  and remember the NAME of Allah.

⟪ar-quote:فَٱذْكُرُوا۟ ٱللَّهَ⟫

and

⟪ar-quote:وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ بُكْرَةًۭ وَأَصِيلًۭا⟫

⟪ar-quote:وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ وَتَبَتَّلْ إِلَيْهِ تَبْتِيلًۭا⟫

So the Quran referes to Allah and the name of Allah as two separte entities. Sometimes we are asked to approach Allah directly. sometimes we are asked to approach him through his name. The point is that we know Allah himself is glorified. but the Quran teaches us that his names are glorified as well! So if the name of Allah is glorified.  then how much more glorified must Allah himself be! If Allah's name is so glorified. then how much more glorified must Allah himself be. If Allah's name is blessed. then how much more blessed must Allah himself be. If the name of Allah is worth of such remembrance. then how much more worthy of remembrance must Allah himself be!

Now the Quran never tells us to worship the name of Allah. It always talks about worshipping Allah directly

فَلَآ أَعْبُدُ ٱلَّذِينَ تَعْبُدُونَ مِن دُونِ ٱللَّهِ وَلَكِنْ أَعْبُدُ ٱللَّهَ ٱلَّذِى يَتَوَفَّىٰكُمْ

Quran did not say.

ِ وَلَكِنْ أَعْبُدُ اسم ٱللَّهَ ٱلَّذِى يَتَوَفَّىٰكُمْ

Similarly the ultimate praise الحمد  is never given to the name of Allah. The ultimate praise is always associated directly with Allah himself. So the Quran says:

الحمد للہ رب العلمین

The quran does not say.

الحمد اسمِ اللہ رب العلمین

so worship and ultimate praise ONLY belongs to Allah himself. not to his name. But تبارک and تسبیح and تذکر . these can belong to both Allah and the name of Allah. We can say we glorify, and exalt Allah.  and the name of Allah. we can say blessed is Alah. and the name of Allah. we can say. we remember Allah and the name of Allah. but we only worship Allah. AND we only praise Allah!

So the reason we have بسم اللہ . is because simply to mention Allah's name is an act of glory. simply to mention Allah's name is an act of acquiring His blessings. simply to mention Allah's name is a way to remember him. and that's why

سَبِّحِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ

تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ

وَٱذْكُرِ ٱسْمَ رَبِّكَ

and therefore also بسم اللہ . with the name of Allah we begin. Because the mere mention of Allah's name is a blessings in and of itself. simply mentioning allah's name attracts his blessings his barakh in our lives.

but when it comes to actual worship it is أَعْبُدُ ٱللَّهَ  and when it comes to actual praise it is الحمد للہ .

### Barakah

⟪ar-quote:أنی اذا اُطِعتُ رَضِیتُ. وأذا رَضِیتُ بَارَکتُ. وَ لَیسَ لِبَرَکَتِی نِھَایَۃ⟫

When you obey me it pleases me. when I am pleased. I bless you. and there is no limit to my blessings.

Now what is the purpose of saying the Basmallah before we begin something? In the last Ayah of Surah AlRehman. Allah AWJ says.

⟪ar-quote:تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ ذِى ٱلْجَلَلِ وَٱلْإِكْرَامِ⟫
The name of Allah. the name of your master. who is glorious and benevolent. his name is full of barakah. The name of Allah. is full of barakah.تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ

. But Allah does not mention in this ayah. which name is full of barakah. right? It just said the name of your maser is full of Barakah. But what did this surah begin with? AlRehman! And what is the first attribute of Allah mentioned in the Basmallah? Bismillahi. AL-REHMAN. AlRaheem. So Allah is telling us something about the word AlRehman. In Surah Rehaman. allah is saying that this name of Allah that I began with. meaning AlRehman. is full of barakah.

But we also know that Allah himself is full of barakah. Because he says it in the Quran.

⟪ar-quote:تبرک اللہ احسن الخالقین⟫

Your Allah is full of barakh who is the best of creators!

but in this last ayah of Surah AlRehman . he's not saying تبرک اللہ . he's not talking about himself. He is talking about his name. He says. تَبَرَكَ ٱسْمُ رَبِّكَ  . The name . AlRehman. of your master is full of Barakah. So Allah is full of Barakah. and His name AlRehman is full of barakah. you understand? Now when we recite the Basmallah. do we have these two names in that ayah? Bismi ALLAHI ALREHMAN AlRaheem. Both Allah and AlRehman. both names of Barakah . is used in the Basmallah.

So the reason we recite the Basmallah. the reason we mention Allah's name before beginnig a task. is for Barakah. This Basmallah is SO FULL of Barakah. that the mention of it spills out that barakah into the task that we about to perform. And by reciting the Basmallah before every task we are about to peroform. we are intentionally asking Allah to bless the task with the barakah of his names in the Basmallah.

Now there is no word in the English language that can full encmpass the meaning of the word Barakah. So we need to understand this word barakah. through certain concepts. In Arabaic. Barakah is defined as.

⟪ar-quote:البرکۃُ النَّماَءُ وَ الزِّیَادَۃ⟫

The first meaning of barakh is growth. something that rises. something that increases. makes progress. something that goes further and further and increases فوق التوقع  beyond expectations. If you plant a seed in the ground. how many trees do you expect? Just one! But if you put one seed in the ground. you get 10 trees. with fruits producing hundreds of thousands of seeds. that is barakah. You planted one seed and eventually got thousands of seeds. that's a growth beyond expectations. that is what you call barakah.  Barakah means. logic says I should get one tree but I got a whole forest. how did that happen? that's barakah. Also what is the comparison of a tree with a seed? There is no comparison. it is beyond comparison. A seed is tiny. a tree is huge. a seed is delicate. a tree is firm. a seed has no value. a tree bears hundreds upon hundreds of fruits. season after season after season. for years and years and years. If you really think about it. what we get from a tree. compared to a seed. there is no comparison. Yet that entire tree came from that one seed. SubhanAllah! That is barakah. unprecedented growth. unlimited increase.

They say أبترکت السمآء  means when rain keeps on coming and keeps on coming. so continuinty is another characteristic of the word barakah. something that stays stationary.

You cook food for 2 people. suddenly 10 guests show up at your door. You all sit down to eat. and from that same food for 2 people. 12 people eat and they leave completely satisified. that is barakah. That's not logical. you only cooked for 2 people. it should not have been enough to satisfy 12 people. but it completely satisfies them. how did that happen? That's barakah. This acutally happened during the time of Ali bin Sydena Suleman QR

I started this session with 5 people. now I have more poeple in the group than skype allows. how did that happen? I did not do anything. I did not go out inviting people. Yet I ended up with so many more poeople in the group. this is barakah. why? Because we are mentioning Allah's name. because we are talking about Allah and AlRehman and AlRaheem.

So the meaning of barakah is growth or increase beyond expectations. Barakah is also used in the Arabic language. for example the Arab would say. ⟪ar:أِذا أَناَخَ الْجَمَل⟫ . When the camel settles on the ground. and it doesn't move or budge. That is also barakah. And this is really beautifull. Because when you grow something. and you grow it too much.  I'll give an example so you can understand. when kids play with legos. they build up this huge tower. which is just block upon block upon block right? Now as the tower is getting tall. does it become more stable? or does it become less stable? It becomes less stable. the taller the tower. the less stable it becomes. It will eventually fall and break. and there will be no tower anymore. isn't that true?

So when something increases rapidly. and increase too much. it becomes less stable. But when something has barakah. it means. that something will increases. and keep increasing beyond expectations. yet remains as stable as a camel sunk in the sand. SubhanAllah!  In other words don't think this increase will go away. its not unstable increase.

We know about unstable increase when we look all around us. our economy goes up really fast. and then what happens? It comes down really fast. there are governments that take over really fast. and then disappear really fast as well. Look at the fashion industry. there are trends that pickup really fast. and then disappear just as fast. something else takes its place. But Allah says barakah is soemthing that increases but it remains stable. it stays. it doesnt go away.

And allah says his name is full of barakh. what does that mean? Means Allah's name and AlRehmans name is being mentioned. since the day creation came into existence. and it only increases and grows with every single passing moment. and it will continue to grow till the very end of creation. Allah and his name.  will remanin forever. because they are full of barakah. worshipers come and go. but the one that is worshipped remains. people who glorify the names of Allah come and go. many came before us. many will come after us. we will all go away. but the glory of Allah will ALWAYS remain.  This is the barakh of Allah's name.

BARR is optimistic in nature

And what does this mean to us? How do we take advanatage of this in our daily lives? It means that we mention Allah's name . when we recite the basmallah. that contains the 2 names of Allah that are full of barakah. when we call upon the barakah of these names. then whatever we do. it will produce good. and it will produce good that will be more than expected . its growth will continue . and it will not disappear. Not only that. it will also be stable. It will keep going and going and going.

Because of this Basmallah. everyone single muslim is supposed to be an optimist. EVEN if the task at hand apparently fails. from that failure there will be growth. the temporary failure will produce spiritual growth and lead to bigger and better tasks.

And because the name of Allah was mentioned before we started the task.  with the intention of calling upon his barakah. that task will be recorded in our book of deeds. and its reward will keep accumulating for the after life. And this is because the very mention of the name of Allah has now made it an act of worship. so now if it takes me 10 hours to complete that task. I just did 10 hours of worship. Just by reciting the Basmallah at the beginning of the task. The time it takes me to complete it is earning me rewards. and after I have completed the task. the effect of what I've produced is going to keep earning rewards for me as long as it is fulfilling its purpose. Just think about that. Reciting one basmallah. with the right intention. and look at the amount of reward it accumulates. So Basmallah before a task. is the seed of barakah that we plant. which then blossoms into thousands upon thousands of trees bearing uncountable fruits of rewards for us. SubhanAllah!

Every single good deed is an act of barakah. you help one single person. you teach one single person. and you don't know. what if that person ends up becoming a great scholar?. He ends up teaching thousands of students. and you keep getting a share of his reward in all his accomplishments. as long as he is teaching and students are benefitting from him. and then some of those students beome teachers and they spread that knowledge. and the reward for ALL of this is accumulating in your book of deeds. because all of this started with the seed you planted. because you started that person on his journey. This is barakah!

All by reciting the Basmallah before beginning a good task. We cannot calculate teh results that stem from the Basmallah. because they are from Allah. and they will grow and grow beyond human expectation . common sense. logic. mathematics cannot capture it within it. they cannot encompass it.

when something has barakah they say

### اللہ

Now let's take a look at the word Allah. Why did Allah choose this name to be his primary name? Not just in the basmallah. but also in numerous other places in the Quran. over 3500 times, the word Allah is used in the Quran. There is no other name of Allah that even comes close to the quantity of times that this name is mentioned.

what's the meaning of this beautiful divine name? Allah! It is the first name mentioned in the Quran . in the first surah AlFateha. بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم، الحمد للہ رب العالمین . and it is also the name mentioned in the last surah of the Quran. Surah AnNaas. الہ الناس . And even in our daily lives. Allah is the primary name we use in . We say Oh Allah give me this. Oh Allah help me with this. Oh Allah protect me from that. We used His actual name . His most glorified name when we are addressing Him or referring to him in our daily lives.

Now lets look at what this name means. and why did our creator. why did our master choose this name for Himself? And this is not a name that is unique to our religion of Islam. Quite the contrary. this is the name that Allah chose for himself and mentioned it in every past scripture. even in the old and new testiments. we find the name Allah. in its hebrew form. In the old testement. we find that god refers to himself as eloh أِلَوہ. and ألوھیم . Allah and Allahumma. and in the new testiment as well. When they crucified Eisa (AS). the bible records his words as.

الائی الائی لما سبختنی  الائی الائی لما ترکتنی

My Allah My Allah why did you abandon me?

Even the nabateans. that are a very ancient race. that existed 6000 years ago. even in the nabatean script. the ultimate god is called Allah. the name is allah. These nabateans had many idols. they had many many idols of all these various gods. but they did not have an idol or a physical form of this god Allah. In other words even they realized that this Allah is too holy for them to draw. because this is the god of all gods.

So the name Allah is in fact the primary name that is not specific to Islam. but every past religion, revelation and scripture. throughout the ages. to all civilizations and to all prophets.

---

---

ILAH ALLAH - NISBATAIN

So Allah is ahad and he is wahid. these are called nisbatain. the 2 attributions. نسبت اعلی اند نسبت ادنی . the greater attribution and the lower attribution. They are both correct. but one is greater than the other. I'll give you an example.  A bulb turns on and lights the room. You can look at the effect and you can look at the cause. What is the effect? The room lights up. there is brightness. there is heat. there is a glow. that's all the effect of the bulb turning on. and you say WOW that is so amazing!! What are you praising? You're praising the effect produced by the bulb turning on.  But another way to look at it. is focus on the cause. what caused the bulb to light up? Oh it was not the bulb itself. but the electricity. that heated the filament inside the bulb . that caused it to glow so bright that it lit up the entire room. and when you realize this you again say. WOW that is so amazing!!! Same statement again. but this time not because of the effect. but because of the CAUSE that produced the effect. So you said WOW that is so amazing by observing the effect. and you said WOW that is so amazing by observing the cause. they're both accurate. but the amazement over the cause is of a higher rank. than the amazmenet over the effect. You understand? You can appreciate the cause and you can appreciate the effect.  but the appreciation of the cause is of a higher rank than the appreciation of the effect. why? Because if there was no cause. there would be no effect!  if there was no cause. there would be no effect! So then in essence the praise . the amazement is actually ONLY for the cause and not for the effect. right? Your appreciation of the effect becomes embedded in the appreciation of the cause. You just can appreciate the power of the electricity and the internal design of the bulb. that in itself will contain the appreciation of the bulb turning on and lighting up a room.  Does that make sense?

So Ahad and Wahid. are both attributions. but ahad is greater in rank than the wahid. why? Because Ahad. is the cause and Wahid is the effect. Wahid or one . exists in the physical dimension. If I ask you how many Allah's do you believe in? You will have to tell me. you believe in ONE allah. But why is he one? He is one because he is unique. because when something is unique. it can only be what? It can only be one!  If there were more than one of that thing. it would no longer be unique. So Allah is one. he is wahid . because he is Ahad first. So He is Ahad first. unique first.  and that's what makes him Wahid. that's what makes him one.  So Ahad is the cause and wahid is the effect.  And because of that from a tawheed point of view. we believe in Allah to be Ahad. We choose the cause. because we know. that the cause will inevitably translate into the effect. of one.

---

In the arabic language there is this thing called the 'Ishtiqaaq'. Ishtiqaaq means that a word is based on another word. it came from some where else. for example you may have heard the word Aalim. its mushtaq. it is derived from another word. Ilm. meaning knowledge. so you have one word derived from another word. it has origin or roots somewhere else. This kind of word is called Mushtaq. . meaning it is a word. but its origin is some other word. it is based on another word.

Then there are words that are original. you cannot trace them back to another word. they are the way they are. and there is no going back. these are originals. untraceable words. and these are called اسماء الجامدۃ . jamid means. solid. there are no building blocks to it. So it is like comparing a wall to a boulder. A wall is made up of bricks. it is a whole made up of parts. but a boulder is a boulder. it is not made up of anything else. it is one solid lump of mass. so Ism Jamid is not made up of parts. but Ism mushtaq is made up of parts. Now which is the cause and which is the effect?  Jamid is the cause and mushtaq is the effect. because Alim exists. only because Ilm exists.

So now why am I telling you all this? I'm telling you all this in order to explain the word Allah to you. Allah is a very unique word. There is no other word in the entire Arabic language that matches this pattern. It is the only word that is both Jamid and it is Mushtaq. It is both cause and effect. both at the same time. So the word Allah has 2 attributions. just as the tawheed of Allah has 2 attributions. there is a higher attribution which is jamid and a lower attribution which is mushtaq.

Let's start with the mushtaq . in our example. the wall that is made up of bricks.  From this perspective. the word Allah is dervied from the word Ilah.

what does this divine name Allah mean? I'm going to go over some of the meanings.

Mushtaq

The name Allah comes from the root word وَلِھَا. waleha means to become astounded. to become astonished. to become amazed. it is as if the person who tries to think of Allah will become amazed and astonished. That you cannot understand who is Allah SWT. Allah is the one that if you try to comprehend Him . you will fail. if you try to walk towards him. you will tire yourself out but never reach him. if you let your thoughts and imaginations fly towards him. you will lose your wings. but not reach him. Allah is an entity that is beyond our comprehension.

مولانا علی کے اقوال

another interpretation of Waliha is to lose ones mind because of the loss of a beloved. That's why in Arabic the mother who loses her son is called مُوَلَّا . this is mother who is suffereing the extreme pain and grief over the loss of her child. she is called مُوَلَّا . now how does thsi relate to the name allah? The one who does not have allah in his life. he is suffering from this type of ultimate grief and madness. the one who does not believe in allah. the one who does not have a connection with Allah it is as if he is going to lose his mind because there is nothing in his life to give him value. to give him meaning. if you don't believe in allah. if you don't ahve a concept of a god in your life. then your life has no purpose. so this is one interpretation that is given.

Another interepreation is that the name Allah comes from  اَلَہَ یَعلُہُ . and alaha literally means to worship. so Ilah is the entity that is the focus of worship and obedience. That's one meaning of the word ALAHA. another mening is the one who you turn to for protection . to turn to for refuge. and therefore allah is the one that each and every created being must turn to for protection . they must turn to for refuge. that no one can exist without turnign to Allah for their every single need. and this is also the meaning of hte name الصمد. Samad is the one that every being turns to for every need. and he himself has no needs.

Another interprtation of the name Allah coms from اَلِہَ  which is used for a child that is thirsty for the milk of its mother. and is desperately crying for it. that's Aliha. and the verbal meaning dervied from it is. the one to whom people desperately turn in need of help. Ilah or Ilha. actually the masdar form is the one people turn to in help in desperation.

So based on this scholars debate that Ilah is the one who is to be worshiped. who is to be obeyed and the one to whom people turn to in desperation. there is no where else to turn but Allah.

it comes from the words لاَہَ یَلِیہُ. and this means to be raised up! therefore the one who believes in Allah . he has raised himself up. in this world and in the next world. the one who believes in allah . he will be honored . in this life and the after life.

Allah comes from the root word Ilaah. Ilaah is a generic term close to the word God. Very rich word, it is a composite word and it has a slew of meanings.

The word Ilah means an entity that is worthy of worship. a Diety.

Ilah is also the object of devotion and love

Ilah is someone you turn to in desperate times

Ilah is also someone you are passionately in love with that you cannot stop thinking about. The word love is already embedded in the word ilah.

And literally speaking. the word Ilah me something you lean on . When you're exhausted and you lean on something, that thing is literally called الہ

Now the word Ilah is generic. there are several people I could love. several people I could turn to for help in desperate times.  I could be in love with multiple people in a lifetime. I love someone intenselly. things go bad. I can then fall in love with someone else. So the word Ilah is a generic term that could appy to multiple entities.

But when I apply the definite article to the word Ilah. when I add the alamate ma'arifa AL to Ilah. then that particular Ilah becomes Allah. So Allah. is actually THE Ilah. Allah is AL + Ilah. they both fuse together to form the word Allah.  The Al adds the clause of exclusivity to this Ilah. Now Ilah is no longer generic. it's an exclusive Allah. What does that mean? It means Allah is the ONLY one I will love. Allah is the ONLY one I will turn to for help in desperate times. Allah is the only one I am going to madly and passionately in love with.  Allah is the ONLY one I will fully and completely lean on.

---

### Jamid

Allah is the universal word for Allah. and it is not a derivate of another word. Allah is the word. Allah chose for himself in every other language. and it is the name he revealed as his proper name to all the messengers in all languages. So on the surface this sounds like more like a spiritual belief thing while the other sound like a linguistic reality. but there are actually linguistic evidence for this as well. And I want to discuss at least a couple of them.

Now we said that the mushtaq Allah. is actually a composite of two words. Al and Ilah. Now in the Arabic language when you call someone . you use the word Ya. For example Ya Walad. Ya Rajul. But in the arabic language. I cannot add the definite article AL to a word when I use YA. So I cannot say YA Al-Walad. or YA Al-Rajul. that would not make sense. that would be grammatically wrong. I can't even use it for his 99 adjectives. Even though in their original form. the attributes have an AL associated with them. We have ALRehman. AlRaheem. AlMalik. AlQuddooos. right?  But when I call upon these attributes. using YA. I have to drop the AL.

I cannot say YA Al-RAHEEM. I have to say Ya Raheem. I cannot say YA Al-Rehman. I have to say YA Rehman. YA Malik. Ya quddoos. Ya Momin. Ya Mohaimin. So even when referring to Allahs attributes I can't use the AL with any of them. But when we call Allah what do we say? We say YA Allah. which we know is actually . YA Al-Ilah. But we do that all the time. So in this linguistic sense. Allah no longer remains a mustaq. it no longer remains a compositive word. it become a jamid. a solid word. Because when we say YA Allah. clearly the AL is still there. and if its there . then its there because its not really an Al. Its part of the actual word itself.  If it wasn't the case. we would call him YA Ilah. the AL would have to be droppped. but we don't do that. we call him Ya Allah. so that means the Al is part of his name.

Secondly. the word Allah is not used generically anywhere in the Quran. as an attribute. Because Ilah or Ilahiyat is an attribute. But in the Quran He is not referred to as the Ilah. He is directly referred to as Allah. And the greatest proof is in the basmallah itself. the ayah says بسم اللہ الرحمن الرحیم . I begin with the name Allah who is Rehman and Raheem. Rehman and Raheem are descriptions. but Allah is the one being described. Allah is the noun and the Rehman and Raheem are the adjectives. Allah is the noun. rab Alalameen. AlRehman AlRaheem. malik yaumid deen. these are all adjectives . therefore Allah is the original name itself. its a jamid.

Then in the context of Surah Ikhlaas. we see that the disbelievers asked the messenger SAS . Tell us who is your lord? Who is your master? Whenever a question is asked. who is he? who do you worship? what do you worship? You don't answer with the descriptions. you always start with the name. So this surah begins. ھو اللہ احد اللہ الصمد . Ahad can be a description. Samad can be a description . but Allah itself is the proper name.

So this word defies all grammatical principles. We break the norm of the arabic language for this word. and ONLY for this word.  It defies all gramatical principles of the Arabic language. For that reason alone it is considered universal. a jamid.

Another . more of a side note. as I mentioned that ALlah was used in all previous languages. it was used in Hebrew. aramaic. and all previous languages. So then was this word Allah a foreign word imported into the Arabic language? Well the grammatical proof for that is. when a foreign word is brought into the Arabic language. you cannot use a kasra. (zer) on it. that's a grammatical rule. So If Allah is a foreign word. then we can have Allahu. we can have Allaha. but we cannot have. Allahee. Thats according to the principles of Arabic grammar. ممنوع من الصرف .

### Seeking Help

The ‘B’ [بِ] in Bismillah is a ‘B’ [ب] of Isti’anah (استعانة), which means ‘seeking help’. So, we are empowering ourselves by seeking Allah’s help before starting an action.

### Incomplete Sentence

Allah left the phrase “Bismillah” as an incomplete sentence. When we say “With the name of Allah,” the verb or action is missing from the sentence. It is not included because the context of where it is used completes the meaning. For instance, when we say Bismillah before reading, the context/intention delivers the meaning as “With the name of Allah, I begin reading.” Therefore, the phrase can be used in different situations.

### Before the Action

Scholars also say that the phrase Bismillah should come before the action. Although it is acceptable as a sentence construction to say, for example, “I read with the name of Allah,” there are two reasons why Bismillah should come first (i.e. “With the name of Allah, I read”):
- To seek blessings by beginning with the name of Allah first and not your action.
- To express the fact that the action is only for Allah. In Arabic language, when you delay the verb, it means exclusivity. So, when we place our action/verb after “With the name of Allah,” it means beginningexclusively with Allah’s Name, seeking His Help alone and solely for His Sake. The Basmalah is used for three primary reasons:

Ikhlaas (Sincerity) – the action is for His Sake alone;

Barakah – seeking His help/blessing for the action;

Qabool (Acceptance) – that Allah accepts and is pleased with our action.

## Meaning of the name 'Allah'

### Linguistic or Literal Meaning

The term 'Allah' is derived from a contraction of the Arabic definite article al- "the" and ilāh "deity, god" to al-lāh meaning "the [sole] deity, God." [Encyclopedia of Islam]

The linguistic meaning of the name of Allah is 'the [sole] deity that deserves to be worshiped'. The word ‘Allah’ comes from the root aliha ya’lahu (bi ma’na “abada ya’budu”). He is the ultimate being who is worthy of being worshipped.

### Greatest Name

It is said [2] that ‘Allah’ is His Greatest Name, because it is referred to when describing Allah by the various attributes. For instance, Allah said:

هُوَ اللَّهُ الَّذِى لاَ إِلَـهَ إِلاَّ هُوَ عَالِمُ الْغَيْبِ وَالشَّهَـدَةِ هُوَ الرَّحْمَـنُ الرَّحِيمُ

He is Allah , other than whom there is no deity, Knower of the unseen and the witnessed. He is the Entirely Merciful, the Especially Merciful.

هُوَ اللَّهُ الَّذِى لاَ إِلَـهَ إِلاَّ هُوَ الْمَلِكُ الْقُدُّوسُ السَّلَـمُ الْمُؤْمِنُ الْمُهَيْمِنُ الْعَزِيزُ الْجَبَّارُ الْمُتَكَبِّرُ سُبْحَـنَ اللَّهِ عَمَّا يُشْرِكُونَ

He is Allah , other than whom there is no deity, the Sovereign, the Pure, the Perfection, the Bestower of Faith, the Overseer, the Exalted in Might, the Compeller, the Superior. Exalted is Allah above whatever they associate with Him.

هُوَ اللَّهُ الْخَـلِقُ الْبَارِىءُ الْمُصَوِّرُ لَهُ الاٌّسْمَآءُ الْحُسْنَى يُسَبِّحُ لَهُ مَا فِى السَّمَـوَتِ وَالاٌّرْضِ وَهُوَ الْعَزِيزُ الْحَكِيمُ

He is Allah , the Creator, the Inventor, the Fashioner; to Him belong the best names. Whatever is in the heavens and earth is exalting Him. And He is the Exalted in Might, the Wise. [Quran, 59:22-24]

Hence, Allah mentioned several of His Names as Attributes for His Name ‘Allah’. Similarly, Allah said,

وَللَّهِ الأَسْمَآءُ الْحُسْنَى فَادْعُوهُ بِهَا

And (all) the Most Beautiful Names belong to Allah, so call on Him by them. [Quran, 7:180]

## How the Prophet (ﷺ) recited the Quran

Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him), when asked about the recitation of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, said:

"His recitation would be elongated, then he recited 'بسم الله الرحمان الرحيم' elongating Bismillah, elongating Ar-Rahman and elongating Ar-Rahim."[Sahih Al-Bukhari; 6/513, no. 566]

⟪ar-quote:لَمْ تَرَكَ الْعُيُونُ؟ فَتُخْبِرَ عَنْكَ! بَلْ كُنْتَ قَبْلَ الْوَاصِفِينَ مِنْ خَلْقِكَ،⟫

آنکھوں میں کہاں اتنی قوت کہ تیرا جلوہ دیکھ سکے اور تیری خبر پہنچا سکے؟ بلکہ تو تیری صفات بیان کرنے والوں سے پہلے موجود تھا۔

⟪ar-quote:لَمْ تَخُلُقِ الْخَلْقَ لِوَحْشَة، وَلاَ اسْتَعْمَلْتَهُمْ لِمَنْفَعَة⟫

تو نے وحشت کی وجہ سے یہ دنیا خلق نہیں فرمائی، اور نہ اپنے کسی فائدے کے لئے بنائی

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ يَسْبِقُكَ مَنْ طلَبْتَ، وَلاَ يُفْلِتُكَ مَنْ أَخَذْتَ،⟫

جسے تو پکڑنا چاہے تجھ سے بھاگ نہیں سکتا، اور جسے تو پکڑ لے تیری گرفت سے نکل نہیں سکتا،

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَ يَنْقُصُ سُلْطَانَكَ مَنْ عَصَاكَ، وَلاَ يَزِيدُ في مُلْكِكَ مَنْ أَطَاعَكَ،⟫

تیری نافرمانی کر کے کوئی تیری سلطنت گھٹا نہیں سکتا، اور تیری اطاعت کر کے کوئی تیری سلطنت بڑھا نہیں سکتا

⟪ar-quote:وَلاَيَرُدُّ أَمْرَكَ مَنْ سَخِطَ قَضَاءَكَ، وَلاَيَسْتَغْنِي عَنْكَ مَنْ تَوَلَّى عَنْ أَمْرِكَ⟫

جو تیرے فیصلہ کی مخالفت کرے اسے بدل نہیں سکتا اور جو تیرے حکم سے منہ موڑے تیرے بغیر رہ نہیں سکتا

⟪ar-quote:كُلُّ سِرٍّ عِنْدَكَ عَلاَنِيَةٌ، وَكُلُّ غَيْب عِنْدَكَ شَهَادَةٌ⟫

تیرے سامنے ہر راز عیاں ہے، اور تیرے سامنے ہر غائب موجود ہے۔
